## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces (e.g., cubic terms in x), nonlinear damping (e.g., v*x² or v³), or time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic driving force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = x * (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = x * (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (parametric + nonlinear)
- Generalized nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (combined effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium; even powers (x²) break this symmetry
- Position-dependent damping terms like v*x² indicate energy dissipation rate depends on amplitude — characteristic of van der Pol type dynamics
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms additive to the acceleration, independent of state variables
- Hardening springs correspond to x³ terms with same sign as x term; softening springs have opposite sign
- Limit cycle behavior requires terms where damping changes sign depending on amplitude, e.g., v*(c0 + c1*x²) with opposite signs on c0 and c1
- Parametric excitation manifests as multiplicative coupling between x and periodic time functions, unlike additive driving
- Conservative (Hamiltonian) nonlinear oscillators have acceleration depending only on x with no v or t dependence
- Velocity-cubed terms (v³) model fluid drag at higher Reynolds numbers, providing amplitude-dependent dissipation
